GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) is:
$$f(x,t) = -1.15357x - 1.15357x\exp(-|x|) + 0.42262\sin(t)$$

The key structural feature is the term $x\exp(-|x|)$, which involves the product of $x$ with an exponential of $-|x|$. Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce this term.

**Key observations about $x\exp(-|x|)$:**
- This function is odd in $x$
- It behaves like $x$ near $x=0$ and decays to 0 as $|x| \to \infty$
- Its Taylor series has infinitely many terms involving all odd powers of $x$ (due to $|x|$)

**Polynomial-based candidates (1, 5, 15, 16, 28, 29, 30, 31, 34, 36, 42, 44):** These use finite polynomials in $x$ (possibly with $x|x|$). A finite polynomial cannot equal $x\exp(-|x|)$ for all $x$, since $x\exp(-|x|) \to 0$ as $|x| \to \infty$ while any nonzero polynomial diverges.

**Rational function candidates (3, 4, 8, 9, 11, 12, 17, 18, 19, 20, 35):** Rational functions like $x/(c+x^2)$ decay as $1/x$ for large $|x|$, while $x\exp(-|x|)$ decays exponentially. These cannot match exactly.

**tanh-based candidates (2, 6, 7, 10, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 39, 40, 41, 47):** $\tanh$ saturates to $\pm 1$, so $\tanh(cx+d)$ plus polynomials cannot reproduce $x\exp(-|x|)$ exactly for all $x$.

**Candidate 38:** $c_0 x + c_1 x^3 + c_2 x^5 + c_3\cos(c_4 t + c_5) + c_6 x\exp(c_7 x^2)$. The term $x\exp(c_7 x^2)$ with $c_7 < 0$ gives $x\exp(-ax^2)$, which is a Gaussian decay, not $\exp(-|x|)$. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidate 31:** Has $x\exp(c_9 x^2)$, same issue as 38.

**Candidate 2:** Has $x\exp(c_9 x^2)$, same issue.

**Candidate 49:** Has $\exp(c_2 x)$ and $\log(c_8\exp(c_9 x)+1)$. Note that $\log(\exp(c_9 x)+1)$ with appropriate constants can approximate $|x|$ (since $\log(e^x+1)$ is the softplus). But $\log(c_8 e^{c_9 x}+1)$ for specific $c_8, c_9$ gives $\log(e^{c_9 x}+1) + \log(c_8)$ only when $c_8$ multiplies the exponential. Actually $\log(c_8 e^{c_9 x}+1)$ is not $|x|$ for all $x$. Even if we could get $|x|$, we'd need $x\exp(-|x|)$, and this candidate doesn't have such a product structure.

**Candidate 44:** $c_0 x^2 + c_1\exp(c_2 x) + c_3 x + c_4 x^3 + c_5 x^5 + c_6\cos(c_7 t+c_8) + c_9 x^7$. A single exponential $\exp(c_2 x)$ is not equivalent to $x\exp(-|x|)$ which behaves differently for positive and negative $x$.

**Candidate 50:** Similar structure with $\exp(c_2 x)$, same issue.

**Candidate 13:** $c_0\sin(c_1 x + c_2) + c_3 x + c_4\cos(c_5 t + c_6)$. Sinusoidal in $x$ cannot match $x\exp(-|x|)$.

**Candidate 33:** Has $\exp(c_4 x)\sin(c_5 t + c_6)$ which couples $x$ and $t$ in a way the GT doesn't (except through separate terms).

No candidate can exactly reproduce the $x\exp(-|x|)$ term for all $x$.

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)

GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT: -1.15357*x - 1.15357*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.42262*sin(t)**

The key components are:
1. A linear term in x
2. x*exp(-|x|) term (note: |x| means this is NOT analytic - it behaves differently for x>0 and x<0)
3. sin(t) term

The function x*exp(-|x|) is the critical non-standard term. Let me analyze its properties:
- For x>0: x*exp(-x) — this is NOT a polynomial, NOT a rational function
- For x<0: x*exp(x) — similarly non-polynomial

Let me check which basis functions could potentially represent x*exp(-|x|).

**Key insight:** x*exp(-|x|) cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials (x, x³, x⁵, x⁷...)
- Rational functions like x/(c+x²)
- x*|x| (which is x²*sign(x))
- tanh(cx) (which saturates)
- sin(cx) or cos(cx)

However, combinations with exp() or specific non-polynomial terms might work. Let me check each candidate.

For candidates with only polynomials + sin/cos(t) + rational functions in x (like x/(a+x²)): These are analytic functions of x (away from poles), but x*exp(-|x|) is not analytic at x=0 (it has a kink in its derivative). So pure polynomial/rational combinations **cannot** match.

Wait - let me reconsider. x*exp(-|x|) actually IS differentiable at x=0 (derivative = 1 at x=0), but the second derivative has a discontinuity. So any candidate that's C² everywhere in x cannot match.

Let me identify candidates with non-analytic or exponential terms:

**Candidates with x*|x|:** 1, 11, 22, 27, 28, 29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 37
- x*|x| = |x|*x = x²*sign(x). This is odd but polynomial-like (C¹ but not C²). However x*exp(-|x|) has exponential decay, not polynomial growth. **Cannot match** with finite polynomial + x*|x| terms.

**Candidates with exp(c*x) or exp(c*x²):** 2, 31, 34, 38, 44, 49, 50
- exp(c*x²): Even in x, while x*exp(-|x|) is odd. Combined with odd polynomial terms, still can't produce x*exp(-|x|).
- exp(c*x): Only works for one sign of x.
- Candidate 2, 31: x*exp(c*x²) — this is odd but Gaussian-type, not matching exp(-|x|).

**Candidates with tanh:** 2, 6, 7, 10, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 39, 40, 41, 47
- tanh is odd, smooth, saturating. Combined with polynomials, cannot produce exp(-|x|) decay.

**Candidate 49:** Has exp(c*x) and log(c*exp(c*x)+1). log(a*exp(bx)+1) is a softplus-like function. For large positive x: ~bx+ln(a), for large negative x: ~0. This is NOT symmetric like |x|.

**Candidate 33:** Has exp(c4*x)*sin(c5*t+c6) — the sin(t) is coupled with exp(x), not separable in the right way. Setting c4=0 kills the exp, leaving polynomial terms.

**Candidate 24:** c6*exp(c7*x)*sin(c8*t+c9) — same issue, exp(x)*sin(t) coupling.

None of these candidates can produce the term x*exp(-|x|) exactly. The function x*exp(-|x|) requires either:
- An explicit exp(-|x|) or exp(-abs(x)) term, or
- Some construction that produces |x| inside an exponential

No candidate has this structure.

After careful analysis, **no candidate matches**.
